## Section 001: Rust Executable Template Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Executable Template Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed no seed line states what this theme actually traces, a template file's growth history, a 141-line six-part template sheet frozen identically across the 202602 and 202603 sweeps, then expanded in 202604 into a 253-line nine-part playbook that nearly doubled the template surface while dropping two artifacts, the join_all concurrency skeleton and the Downloads-path source block
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Executable Template Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the 202604 bundle rebuilt the older skill's template sheet into a playbook for a new skill, so this theme's real content is template evolution, what grew, what survived verbatim, and what was cut, rather than any single file's contents
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Executable Template Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: readers treating the three paths as three template sets miss that they hold one lineage in three snapshots, and template consumers who grab the oldest copy get four skeletons and no layering scaffold where the successor offers seven skeletons and the L1/L2/L3 table

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: triple-counting would overweight the ancestor's choices two-to-one against the successor in any synthesis, inverting the lineage's actual authority direction where the newest snapshot supersedes
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: provenance for this document's statements, all four external URLs stayed unretrieved and confer no current-fact authority

## Section 007: Anti Pattern Registry Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed three corpus-process rows stand where the lineage exhibits template-specific failures, snapshot regression, consuming the frozen ancestor where the successor supersedes it, hollow completion, filling every blank with unmeasurable filler that satisfies shape while defeating doctrine, and skeleton bit-rot, copied test code that no longer compiles against current crates
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each failure follows from what a template is, versioned, fillable, executable, versioning enables regression, fillability enables hollowness, and executability enables rot, the artifact class carries its failure class
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the three decay differently, regression serves outdated menus loudly at copy time, hollowness passes every structural check and surfaces only in review quality, and rot detonates downstream in consumer crates with misdirected blame
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: registry rows for template consumption and maintenance, the anti-patterns the templates test for belong to the reliability theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the three rows with detections, lineage-role checks at citation time for regression, blank-quality sampling against the rewrite table for hollowness, and dated compile checks for rot

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

## Section 010: User Journey Scenario

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed template rows skip the lineage's live tensions, growth versus focus, where the playbook nearly doubled its ancestor and each addition dilutes the sheet's grab-and-go character, concrete versus portable skeletons, where compilable examples freeze crate choices that rot, and example versus quota in the matrix, where seven illustrative rows read as seven obligations to completionist consumers
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each tension is inherent to executable templates, usefulness demands concreteness and coverage, while durability demands smallness and abstraction, and the lineage's one revision moved every axis toward usefulness, accepting the durability costs this theme's probes now watch
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: each chosen pole's cost is already identifiable, the doubled sheet takes longer to navigate, the frozen tokio and proptest idioms carry unverified compilability, and the seven-row example needs its own smallest-useful-set disclaimer to fight quota reading, a disclaimer the ancestor's four-row version did not need
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: tuning the lineage's template design decisions, doctrine-content tradeoffs belong to the themes the templates operationalize

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed symbol-count boundary misprices lineage work, whose units are per-audit genealogy cost, one diff, two block spot checks, and a map walk across 535 total lines, per-revision cost, the bounded update of changelog, correspondences, and sync points when a new snapshot lands, and per-authorship cost, the packet chain's fill time, which belongs to the consumer's task budget, not this theme's
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the theme's own work is again metadata upkeep at minutes scale, while the one expensive event, a template revision, is rare and bounded by the changelog's pre-existing structure, the same cheap-standing-work-caps-episodic-risk economics the entrypoint theme found
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the mispricing risk is the cluster's usual one, work too small to schedule silently stops, plus one new hazard, revision events look like ordinary edits, and a maintainer who does not recognize a template edit as a lineage event skips the changelog update that keeps every downstream judgment current
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: budgeting lineage upkeep, the Rust work packets the templates produce carry their own budgets in their own tasks
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to restate the model in its three units with the boundary clarified, audit minutes ride the corpus cadence, revision updates are bounded half-days triggered by template edits, and authorship time is out of scope by design
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the lineage adds a unit no sibling theme has, revision recognition, the trigger cost of noticing that an edit is a lineage event, which is nearly free when edits flow through corpus review and unbounded when they do not, so the workload model's real dependency is the corpus's edit-visibility discipline, not any property of the templates themselves

- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to piggyback audits on the corpus cadence and gate template edits through review so revision recognition stays free

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: budgeting lineage upkeep, the Rust work packets the templates produce carry their own budgets in their own tasks
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: restate the model in its three units with the boundary clarified, audit minutes ride the corpus cadence, revision updates are bounded half-days triggered by template edits, and authorship time is out of scope by design

- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the four arise from the lineage's defining properties, versioning enables unrecorded change and resurrection, fillability enables fossilized filler, and compositionality enables severance, each property's shadow is its failure

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed generic records stand beside the templates' own observability teaching, the packet's gate block forcing verification results into fixed reportable positions, the matrix's metric column forcing every test to name what it measures, and the id convention making the whole packet's claim structure mechanically traceable, observability of work rather than observability of systems
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the templates instrument the engineering process the way tracing instruments services, fixed positions, named metrics, and threaded ids are the process equivalents of structured fields, span names, and correlation ids, one discipline at two levels
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: packets without the instrumentation habits degrade review from verification to archaeology, reviewers reconstructing what was claimed and checked from prose, the process equivalent of debugging an unlogged service
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: what the template layer makes observable about work, system-level telemetry doctrine belongs to the reliability and ops themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the two-level parallel explicitly and specify this theme's own records, the audit trail of genealogy checks, compile logs, and the changelog, each dated, each findable

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the template layer's performance chain, measurement methodology depth belongs to the testing and benchmarking themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the chain and its caveat, the skeleton demonstrates threshold-as-code and real packets should upgrade to warm-up, repetition, and percentile reporting when the stakes justify it

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed task-splitting bounds stand beside this lineage's real scale limits, the template chain fits single-packet work and strains at program scale, where many packets need cross-packet id namespaces and shared requirement registries the templates never define, and the lineage structure fits one ancestor-successor edge and strains when revisions multiply into a version tree needing real changelog tooling
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because both limits are namespace exhaustion in disguise, REQ-RUST-001 collides the moment two packets coexist, and hand-walked correspondence maps collide the moment two revisions diverge, flat naming schemes buckling under multiplicity
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: past the packet limit, id-threading integrity breaks corpus-wide because duplicate ids thread falsely across packets, and past the revision limit, unrecorded-revision probability rises with every edit the hand-maintained changelog must catch
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: bounding the template chain and lineage machinery, the doctrine's own scale seams belong to the routed themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to name both limits with triggers, multi-packet programs trigger id namespacing by component or packet prefix, and a second lineage edge triggers changelog tooling beyond the hand-built artifact
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the id-collision limit is invisible in every source file because each snapshot demonstrates exactly one packet, the templates teach a naming convention whose failure mode only exists outside any single document, scale limits of compositional artifacts live in the composition, not the components, which is why no amount of snapshot auditing would ever surface this one
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to prefix requirement ids by component the moment a second packet enters the same program, and adopt the pattern preemptively in multi-team settings
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because both limits are namespace exhaustion in disguise, REQ-RUST-001 collides the moment two packets coexist, and hand-walked correspondence maps collide the moment two revisions diverge, flat naming schemes buckling under multiplicity
